<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Indirect land use change impacts of biofuels</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg/220px-Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg/330px-Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg/440px-Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grande_Sertao_Veredas_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">cerrado</a>.</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amazonie.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Amazonie.jpg/220px-Amazonie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Amazonie.jpg/330px-Amazonie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Amazonie.jpg/440px-Amazonie.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amazonie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>indirect land use change impacts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biofuels" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a></b>, also known as <b>ILUC</b>, relates to the unintended consequence of releasing more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_use,_land-use_change_and_forestry" title="Land use, land-use change and forestry">land-use changes</a> around the world induced by the expansion of croplands for <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a> or <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> production in response to the increased global demand for biofuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WangLetScie_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-WangLetScie-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>As farmers worldwide respond to higher crop prices in order to maintain the global food supply-and-demand balance, pristine lands are cleared to replace the food crops that were diverted elsewhere to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Biofuels%27_production&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Biofuels' production (page does not exist)">biofuels' production</a>. Because natural lands, such as <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a>, store carbon in their soil and <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a> as plants grow each year, clearance of wilderness for new farms translates to a net increase in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>. Due to this change in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_stock" title="Carbon stock">carbon stock</a> of the soil and the biomass, indirect land use change has consequences in the GHG balance of a biofuel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WangLetScie_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-WangLetScie-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lausanne_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lausanne-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OpedFarrel_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-OpedFarrel-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other authors have also argued that indirect land use changes produce other significant social and environmental impacts, affecting biodiversity, water quality, <a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">food prices and supply</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_tenure" title="Land tenure">land tenure</a>, worker migration, and community and cultural stability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lausanne_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lausanne-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyer08_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyer08-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Righelato07_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Righelato07-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="toclimit-3"><div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The estimates of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_intensity" title="Carbon intensity">carbon intensity</a> for a given biofuel depend on the assumptions regarding several variables. As of 2008, multiple <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_cycle_assessment" title="Life cycle assessment">full life cycle</a> studies had found that <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_the_United_States" title="Ethanol fuel in the United States">corn ethanol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">cellulosic ethanol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_Brazil" title="Ethanol fuel in Brazil">Brazilian sugarcane ethanol</a> produce lower greenhouse gas emissions than <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farrel2006_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farrel2006-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USEthanol_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-USEthanol-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang2005_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2005-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang205ppt_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wang205ppt-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA04_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-MLA04-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRTFO_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKRTFO-14">[14]</a></sup> None of these studies, however, considered the effects of indirect land-use changes, and though land use impacts were acknowledged, estimation was considered too complex and difficult to model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WangLetScie_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-WangLetScie-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup> A controversial paper published in February 2008 in <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Sciencexpress</a> by a team led by Searchinger from <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> concluded that such effects offset the (positive) direct effects of both corn and cellulosic ethanol and that Brazilian sugarcane performed better, but still resulted in a small carbon debt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1488" data-file-width="1562" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg/220px-Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg/330px-Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg/440px-Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cloud_forest_mount_kinabalu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysian</a> <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">cloud forest</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the Searchinger team paper, estimation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> from ILUC, together with the <a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">food vs. fuel</a> debate, became one of the most contentious <a href="/wiki/Issues_relating_to_biofuels" title="Issues relating to biofuels">issues relating to biofuels</a>, debated in the <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">popular media</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time0208_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time0208-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time0308_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time0308-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DebateTime_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-DebateTime-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1108_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1108-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA1108_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-RFA1108-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC1008_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC1008-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1108_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1108-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFC042209_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFC042209-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scientific_journal" title="Scientific journal">scientific journals</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WangLetScie_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-WangLetScie-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Righelato07_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Righelato07-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ScienceBiofuel_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ScienceBiofuel-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SearchingResponse_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-SearchingResponse-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORNLletter_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-ORNLletter-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">op-eds</a> and public letters from the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_community" title="Scientific community">scientific community</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OpedFarrel_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-OpedFarrel-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letter27scient_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-letter27scient-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letter170scient_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-letter170scient-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0408_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0408-29">[29]</a></sup> and  the ethanol industry, both American and Brazilian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist0809_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist0809-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LetterCARB_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-LetterCARB-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA03_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA03-32">[32]</a></sup> This controversy intensified in April 2009 when the <a href="/wiki/California_Air_Resources_Board" title="California Air Resources Board">California Air Resources Board</a> (CARB) set rules that included ILUC impacts to establish the <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_fuel_standard#California_Low-Carbon_Fuel_Standard" title="Low-carbon fuel standard">California Low-Carbon Fuel Standard</a> that entered into force in 2011.
</p><p>In May 2009 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a> (EPA) released a <a href="/wiki/Notice_of_proposed_rulemaking" title="Notice of proposed rulemaking">notice of proposed rulemaking</a> for implementation of the 2007 modification of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_Fuel_Standard" title="Renewable Fuel Standard">Renewable Fuel Standard</a> (RFS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> EPA's proposed regulations also included ILUC, causing additional controversy among ethanol producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT0609_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAT0609-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian0609_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian0609-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP0506_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP0506-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jennifer_Kho_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jennifer_Kho-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA_Press_Release_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA_Press_Release-38">[38]</a></sup> EPA's February 3, 2010 final rule incorporated ILUC based on modelling that was significantly improved over the initial estimates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPARuling_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPARuling-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA2010_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPA2010-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">UK</a> <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Transport_Fuel_Obligation" title="Renewable Transport Fuel Obligation">Renewable Transport Fuel Obligation</a> program requires the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Fuels_Agency" title="Renewable Fuels Agency">Renewable Fuels Agency</a> (RFA) to report potential indirect impacts of biofuel production, including indirect land use change or changes to food and other commodity prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRTFO_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-UKRTFO-14">[14]</a></sup> A July 2008 RFA study, known as the Gallager Review, found several risks and uncertainties, and that the "quantification of GHG emissions from indirect land-use change requires subjective assumptions and contains considerable uncertainty", and required further examination to properly incorporate indirect effects into calculation methodologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher0708_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher0708-41">[41]</a></sup> A similarly cautious approach was followed by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. In December 2008 the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> adopted more stringent sustainability criteria for biofuels and directed the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> to develop a methodology to factor in GHG emissions from indirect land use change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU08_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU08-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Studies_and_controversy">Studies and controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Studies and controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles"><span title="The material near this tag may contain information that is not relevant to the article's main topic. (December 2017)">relevant?</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels" title="Talk:Indirect land use change impacts of biofuels">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>
</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="949" data-file-width="1357" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg/290px-BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg/435px-BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg/580px-BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BioethanolsCountryOfOrigin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UK figures for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_intensity" title="Carbon intensity">carbon intensity</a> of bioethanol and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>. Graph assumes all bioethanols are burnt in country of origin and prior cropland was used to grow feedstock. No ILUC effects were included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRTFO_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-UKRTFO-14">[14]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Before 2008, several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_cycle_assessment" title="Life cycle assessment">full life cycle</a> ("Well to Wheels" or WTW) studies had found that <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_the_United_States" title="Ethanol fuel in the United States">corn ethanol</a> reduced transport-related greenhouse gas emissions. In 2007 a <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a> team led by Farrel evaluated six previous studies, concluding that corn ethanol reduced GHG emissions by only 13 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farrel2006_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Farrel2006-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang205ppt_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wang205ppt-12">[12]</a></sup> However, 20 to 30 percent reduction for corn ethanol, and 85 to 85 percent for <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">cellulosic ethanol</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USEthanol_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-USEthanol-10">[10]</a></sup> both figures estimated by Wang from <a href="/wiki/Argonne_National_Laboratory" title="Argonne National Laboratory">Argonne National Laboratory</a>, are more commonly cited. Wang reviewed 22 studies conducted between 1979 and 2005, and ran simulations with Argonne's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GREET_model" title="GREET model">GREET model</a>. These studies accounted for direct land use changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang2005_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2005-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang205ppt_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wang205ppt-12">[12]</a></sup> Several studies of Brazilian sugarcane ethanol showed that sugarcane as feedstock reduces GHG by 86 to 90 percent given no significant land use change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA04_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-MLA04-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRTFO_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-UKRTFO-14">[14]</a></sup> Estimates of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_intensity" title="Carbon intensity">carbon intensity</a> depend on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crop_productivity" title="Crop productivity">crop productivity</a>, agricultural practices, power sources for ethanol distilleries and the energy efficiency of the distillery. None of these studies considered ILUC, due to estimation difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WangLetScie_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-WangLetScie-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup> Preliminary estimates by Delucchi from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis" title="University of California, Davis">University of California, Davis</a>, suggested that carbon released by new lands converted to agricultural use was a large percentage of life-cycle emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Delucchi2006_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Delucchi2006-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Searchinger_and_Fargione_studies">Searchinger and Fargione studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Searchinger and Fargione studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008 Timothy Searchinger, a <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyer</a> from <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Defense_Fund" title="Environmental Defense Fund">Environmental Defense Fund</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> concluded that ILUC affects the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_cycle_assessment" title="Life cycle assessment">life cycle assessment</a> and that instead of saving, both corn and cellulosic ethanol increased carbon emissions as compared to gasoline by 93 and 50 percent respectively. Ethanol from Brazilian sugarcane performed better, recovering initial carbon emissions in 4 years, while U.S. corn ethanol required 167 years and cellulosic ethanol required a 52 years payback period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup> The study limited the analysis a 30-year period, assuming that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_conversion" title="Land conversion">land conversion</a> emits 25 percent of the carbon stored in soils and all carbon in plants cleared for cultivation. Brazil, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> were considered among the overseas locations where land use change would occur as a result of diverting U.S. corn cropland, and it was assumed that new cropland in each of these regions correspond to different types of <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> or <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grassland</a> based on the historical proportion of each converted to cultivation in these countries during the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">
<tbody><tr>
<th align="center" colspan="5" style="background-color: #ccffcc;">Summary of Searchinger et al. <br/>comparison of corn ethanol and gasoline <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">GHG</a> emissions<br/>with and without land use change <br/> (<a href="/wiki/Gram" title="Gram">Grams</a> of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_equivalent" title="Carbon dioxide equivalent">CO<sub>2</sub></a> released per <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megajoule" title="Megajoule">megajoule</a> of energy in fuel)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Searchinger0208_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-Searchinger0208-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SearchingerSM_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-SearchingerSM-45">[45]</a></sup>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Fargione and his team published a separate paper in the same issue of Sciencexpress claiming that clearing lands to produce biofuel feedstock created a carbon deficit. This deficit applies to both direct and indirect land use changes. The study examined six conversion scenarios: <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a> <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>, Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">Cerrado</a> to soybean biodiesel, Brazilian Cerrado to sugarcane ethanol, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysian</a> lowland <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_palm" title="Oil palm">palm</a> biodiesel, Indonesian or Malaysian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peatland" title="Peatland">peatland</a> tropical rainforest to palm biodiesel, and U.S. Central <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grassland</a> to corn ethanol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fargione08_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fargione08-46">[46]</a></sup> The carbon debt was defined as the amount of CO<sub>2</sub> released during the first 50 years of this process of land conversion. For the two most common ethanol feedstocks, the study found that sugarcane ethanol produced on natural cerrado lands would take about 17 years to repay its carbon debt, while corn ethanol produced on U.S. central grasslands would result in a repayment time of about 93 years. The worst-case scenario is converting Indonesian or Malaysian tropical peatland rainforest to palm biodiesel production, which would require about 420 years to repay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fargione08_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fargione08-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversy">Criticism and controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Criticism and controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Searchinger and Fargione studies created controversy in both the <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">popular media</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OpedFarrel_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-OpedFarrel-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time0208_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Time0208-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time0308_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Time0308-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DebateTime_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-DebateTime-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT1108_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1108-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA1108_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-RFA1108-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1108_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1108-21">[21]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Scientific_journal" title="Scientific journal">scientific journals</a>. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zubrin" title="Robert Zubrin">Robert Zubrin</a> observed that Searchinger's "indirect analysis" approach is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pseudo-science" title="Pseudo-science">pseudo-scientific</a> and can be used to "prove anything".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wang and Haq from Argonne National Laboratory claiming:  the assumptions were outdated; they ignored the potential of increased efficiency; and no evidence showed that "U.S. corn ethanol production has so far caused indirect land use in other countries." They concluded that Searchinger demonstrated that ILUC "is much more difficult to model than direct land use changes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WangLetScie_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-WangLetScie-2">[2]</a></sup> In his response Searchinger rebutted each technical objection and asserted that "... any calculation that ignores these emissions, however challenging it is to predict them with certainty, is too incomplete to provide a basis for policy decisions."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SearchingResponse_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-SearchingResponse-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SearchingNFAResponse_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-SearchingNFAResponse-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another criticism, by Kline and Dale from <a href="/wiki/Oak_Ridge_National_Laboratory" title="Oak Ridge National Laboratory">Oak Ridge National Laboratory</a>, held that Searchinger et al. and Fargione et al. "... do not provide adequate support for their claim that bioufuels cause high emissions due to land-use change", as their conclusions depends on a misleading assumption because more comprehensive field research found that these land use changes "... are driven by interactions among cultural, technological, biophysical, economic, and demographic forces within a spatial and temporal context rather than by a single crop market".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORNLletter_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-ORNLletter-26">[26]</a></sup> Fargione et al. responded in part that although many factors contributed to land clearing, this "observation does not diminish the fact that biofuels also contribute to land clearing if they are produced on existing cropland or on newly cleared lands". Searching disagreed with all of Kline and Dale arguments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ORNLletter_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-ORNLletter-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. biofuel industry also reacted, claiming that the "Searchinger study is clearly a 'worst case scenario' analysis ..." and that this study "relies on a long series of highly subjective assumptions ..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NFAResponse_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-NFAResponse-49">[49]</a></sup> Searchinger rebutted each claim, concluding that NFA's criticisms were invalid. He noted that even if some of his assumptions are high estimates, the study also made many conservative assumptions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SearchingNFAResponse_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-SearchingNFAResponse-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SlashandburninBrazil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="330" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/SlashandburninBrazil.jpg/220px-SlashandburninBrazil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/SlashandburninBrazil.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SlashandburninBrazil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Slash and burn forest removal in Brazil.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nelore_cattle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="640" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Nelore_cattle.jpg/220px-Nelore_cattle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Nelore_cattle.jpg/330px-Nelore_cattle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Nelore_cattle.jpg/440px-Nelore_cattle.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nelore_cattle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cattle_ranching" title="Cattle ranching">Cattle ranching</a> in Brazil.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2010, Lapola estimated that planned expansion of Brazilian sugarcane and soybean biofuel plantations through 2020 would replace <a href="/wiki/Rangeland" title="Rangeland">rangeland</a>, with  small direct land-use impact on carbon emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lapola2010_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lapola2010-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mongabay_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mongabay-51">[51]</a></sup> However, the expansion of the rangeland frontier into Amazonian forests, driven by cattle ranching, would indirectly offset the savings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mongabay_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mongabay-51">[51]</a></sup> "Sugarcane ethanol and soybean biodiesel each contribute to nearly half of the projected indirect deforestation of 121,970 km<sup>2</sup> by 2020, creating a carbon debt that would take about 250 years to be repaid...."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lapola2010_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lapola2010-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>The research also found that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_palm" title="Oil palm">oil palm</a> would cause the least land-use changes and associated carbon debt. The analysis also modeled livestock density increases and found that "a higher increase of 0.13 head per hectare in the average livestock density throughout the country could avoid the indirect land-use changes caused by biofuels (even with soybean as the biodiesel feedstock), while still fulfilling all food and bioenergy demands."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lapola2010_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lapola2010-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mongabay_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mongabay-51">[51]</a></sup> The authors conclude that intensification of cattle ranching and concentration on oil palm are required to achieve effective carbon savings, recommending closer collaboration between the biofuel and cattle-ranching sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lapola2010_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lapola2010-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mongabay_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-Mongabay-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>The main <a href="/wiki/UNICA,_Brazil" title="UNICA, Brazil">Brazilian ethanol industry organization</a> (UNICA) commented that such studies missed the continuing intensification of cattle production already underway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>A study by Arima <i>et al.</i> published in May 2011 used spatial regression modeling to provide the first statistical assessment of ILUC for the Brazilian Amazon due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soy" title="Soy">soy</a> production. Previously, the indirect impacts of soy crops were only anecdotal or analyzed through demand models at a global scale, while the study took a regional approach. The analysis showed a strong signal linking the expansion of soybean fields in settled agricultural areas at the southern and eastern rims of the Amazon basin to pasture encroachments for cattle production on the forest frontier. The results demonstrate the need to include ILUC in measuring the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> of soy crops, whether produced for biofuels or other end-uses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arima_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arima-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Arima study is based on 761 municipalities located in the <a href="/wiki/Amaz%C3%B4nia_Legal" title="Amazônia Legal">Legal Amazon of Brazil</a>, and found that between 2003 and 2008, soybean areas expanded by 39,100 km² in the basin's agricultural areas, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">Mato Grosso</a>. The model showed that a 10% (3,910 km²) reduction of soy in old pasture areas would have led to a reduction in deforestation of up to 40% (26,039 km²) in heavily forested municipalities of the Brazilian Amazon. The analysis showed that the displacement of cattle production due to <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_expansion" title="Agricultural expansion">agricultural expansion</a> drives land use change in municipalities located hundreds of kilometers away, and that the Amazonian ILUC is not only measurable but its impact is significant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arima_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Arima-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementation">Implementation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Implementation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_fuel_standard" title="Low-carbon fuel standard">Low-carbon fuel standard</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="California_LCFS">California LCFS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: California LCFS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On April 23, 2009, <a href="/wiki/California_Air_Resources_Board" title="California Air Resources Board">California Air Resources Board</a> (CARB) approved the specific rules and carbon intensity reference values for the <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_fuel_standard#California_Low-Carbon_Fuel_Standard" title="Low-carbon fuel standard">California Low-Carbon Fuel Standard</a> (LCFS) that take effect January 1, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG042409_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFG042409-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT042409_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT042409-57">[57]</a></sup> CARB's rulemaking included ILUC. For some biofuels, CARB identified land use changes as a significant source of additional GHG emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARBproposal_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-ARBproposal-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CARBres0931_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-CARBres0931-58">[58]</a></sup> It established one standard for gasoline and alternative fuels, and a second for diesel fuel and its replacements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CARBruleB_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-CARBruleB-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The public consultation process before the ruling, and the ruling itself were controversial, yielding 229 comments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> ILUC was one of the most contentious issues. On June 24, 2008, 27 scientists and researchers submitted a letter saying, "As researchers and scientists in the field of biomass to biofuel conversion, we are convinced that there simply is not enough hard empirical data to base any sound policy regulation in regards to the indirect impacts of renewable biofuels production. The field is relative new, especially when compared to the vast knowledge base present in fossil fuel production, and the limited analyses are driven by assumptions that sometimes lack robust empirical validation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC08_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC08-61">[61]</a></sup> The New Fuels Alliance, representing more than two-dozen biofuel companies, researchers and investors, questioned the Board intention to include indirect land use change effects into account, wrote "While it is likely true that zero is not the right number for the indirect effects of any product in the real world, enforcing indirect effects in a piecemeal way could have very serious consequences for the LCFS.... The argument that zero is not the right number does not justify enforcing a different wrong number, or penalizing one fuel for one category of indirect effects while giving another fuel pathway a free pass."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC08_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-GCC08-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>On the other side, more than 170 scientists and economists urged that CARB, "include indirect land use change in the lifecycle analyses of heat-trapping emissions from biofuels and other transportation fuels. This policy will encourage development of sustainable, low-carbon fuels that avoid conflict with food and minimize harmful environmental impacts.... There are uncertainties inherent in estimating the magnitude of indirect land use emissions from biofuels, but assigning a value of zero is clearly not supported by the science."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Industry representatives complained that the final rule overstated the environmental effects of corn ethanol, and also criticized the inclusion of ILUC as an unfair penalty to domestic corn ethanol because deforestation in the developing world was being tied to U.S. ethanol production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFC042209_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-SFC042209-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT042409_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT042409-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciAm_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-SciAm-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT042409_2_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT042409_2-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BDigest_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-BDigest-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenM_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-GreenM-68">[68]</a></sup> The 2011 limit for LCFS means that Mid-west corn ethanol failed, unless current carbon intensity was reduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG042409_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-SFG042409-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BDigest_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-BDigest-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN0409_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN0409-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACBee_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-SACBee-70">[70]</a></sup> Oil industry representatives complained that the standard left oil refiners with few options, such as Brazilian sugarcane ethanol, with its accompanying tariff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenM_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-GreenM-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACBee_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-SACBee-70">[70]</a></sup> CARB officials and environmentalists counter that time and economic incentives will allow produces to adapt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenM_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-GreenM-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACBee_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-SACBee-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>UNICA welcomed the ruling,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA01_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA01-71">[71]</a></sup> while urging CARB to better reflect Brazilian practices, lowering their estimates of Brazilian emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA03_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA03-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA01_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA01-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA02_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA02-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>The only Board member who voted against the ruling explained that he had a "hard time accepting the fact that we're going to ignore the comments of 125 scientists", referring to the letter submitted by a group of scientists questioning the ILUC penalty. "They said the model was not good enough ... to use at this time as a component part of such an historic new standard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BDigest_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-BDigest-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN0409_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN0409-69">[69]</a></sup> CARB advanced the expected date for an expert working group to report on ILUC with refined estimates from January 2012 to January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciAm_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-SciAm-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BDigest_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-BDigest-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN0409_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNN0409-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 2009 the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Fuels_Association" title="Renewable Fuels Association">Renewable Fuels Association</a> (RFA) and <a href="/wiki/Growth_Energy" title="Growth Energy">Growth Energy</a>, two U.S. ethanol lobbying groups, filed a lawsuit challenging LCFS' <a href="/wiki/Constitutionality" title="Constitutionality">constitutionality</a>. The two organizations argued that LCFS violated both the <a href="/wiki/Supremacy_Clause" title="Supremacy Clause">Supremacy Clause</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commerce_Clause" title="Commerce Clause">Commerce Clause</a>, jeopardizing the nationwide ethanol market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ1209_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ1209-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC1209_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC1209-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EPA_Renewable_Fuel_Standard">EPA Renewable Fuel Standard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: EPA Renewable Fuel Standard">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_Policy_Act_of_2005" title="Energy Policy Act of 2005">Energy Policy Act of 2005</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_Independence_and_Security_Act_of_2007" title="Energy Independence and Security Act of 2007">Energy Independence and Security Act of 2007</a></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">
<tbody><tr>
<th align="center" colspan="3" style="background-color: #ABCDEF;"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a><br/>Draft <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_cycle_assessment" title="Life cycle assessment">life cycle</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GHG_emissions" title="GHG emissions">GHG emissions</a> reduction results<br/> for different <a href="/wiki/Time_horizon" title="Time horizon">time horizon</a> and discount rate approaches<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAdraft_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAdraft-76">[76]</a></sup><br/>(includes indirect land use change effects)

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3"><small>Notes: (1) Dry mill (DM) plants grind the entire kernel and generally produce<br/> only one primary co-product: <a href="/wiki/Distillers_grains" title="Distillers grains">distillers grains</a> with solubles (DGS).<br/> (2) Best case plants produce wet distillers grains co-product.</small>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Energy_Independence_and_Security_Act_of_2007" title="Energy Independence and Security Act of 2007">Energy Independence and Security Act of 2007</a> (EISA) established new renewable fuel categories and eligibility requirements, setting mandatory <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_cycle_assessment" title="Life cycle assessment">lifecycle</a> emissions limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAdraft_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPAdraft-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA0509_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPA0509-77">[77]</a></sup> EISA explicitly mandated EPA to include "direct emissions and significant indirect emissions such as significant emissions from land use changes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAdraft_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPAdraft-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA0509_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPA0509-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0509_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0509-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>EISA required a 20% reduction in lifecycle GHG emissions for any fuel produced at  facilities that commenced construction after December 19, 2007 to be classified as a "renewable fuel"; a 50% reduction for fuels to be classified as "biomass-based diesel" or "advanced biofuel", and a 60% reduction to be classified as "cellulosic biofuel". EISA provided limited flexibility to adjust these thresholds downward by up to 10 percent, and EPA proposed this adjustment for the advanced biofuels category. Existing plants were <a href="/wiki/Grandfather_clause" title="Grandfather clause">grandfathered</a> in.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAdraft_76-3"><a href="#cite_note-EPAdraft-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA0509_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPA0509-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0509_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0509-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 5, 2009, EPA released a <a href="/wiki/Notice_of_proposed_rulemaking" title="Notice of proposed rulemaking">notice of proposed rulemaking</a> for implementation of the 2007 modification of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_Fuel_Standard" title="Renewable Fuel Standard">Renewable Fuel Standard</a>, known as RFS2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0509_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0509-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAproposal_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAproposal-79">[79]</a></sup> The draft of the regulations was released for public comment during a 60-day period, a public hearing was held on 9 June 2009, and also a workshop was conducted on 10–11 June 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA0509_77-3"><a href="#cite_note-EPA0509-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0509_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0509-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>EPA's draft analysis stated that ILUC can produce significant near-term GHG emissions due to land conversion, but that biofuels can pay these back over subsequent years. EPA highlighted two  scenarios, varying the time horizon and the <a href="/wiki/Discounted_cash_flow" title="Discounted cash flow">discount rate</a> for valuing emissions. The first assumed a 30-year time period uses a 0 percent discount rate (valuing emissions equally regardless of timing). The second scenario used a 100-year time period and a 2% discount rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAdraft_76-4"><a href="#cite_note-EPAdraft-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA0509_77-4"><a href="#cite_note-EPA0509-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0509_78-4"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0509-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>On the same day that EPA published its notice of proposed rulemaking, President Obama signed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Directive" title="Presidential Directive">Presidential Directive</a> seeking to advance biofuels research and commercialization. The Directive established the Biofuels Interagency Working Group, to develop policy ideas for increasing investment in next-generation fuels and for reducing their environmental footprint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT0609_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-LAT0609-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WH0509_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-WH0509-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0509_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0509-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sciam0509_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sciam0509-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="640" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg/220px-Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg/330px-Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg/440px-Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Combine-harvesting-corn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Maize</a> is the main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feedstock" title="Feedstock">feedstock</a> for the production of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_the_United_States" title="Ethanol fuel in the United States">ethanol fuel in the U.S.</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG/220px-Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG/330px-Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG/440px-Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sugarcane_harvest_Piracicaba_05_2009_5783.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">Sugarcane</a> is the main feedstock for the production of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_Brazil" title="Ethanol fuel in Brazil">ethanol fuel in Brazil</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The inclusion of ILUC in the proposed ruling provoked complaints from ethanol<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT0609_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-LAT0609-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian0609_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian0609-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP0506_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-WP0506-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jennifer_Kho_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jennifer_Kho-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA_Press_Release_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA_Press_Release-38">[38]</a></sup> and biodiesel producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Several environmental organizations welcomed the inclusion of ILUC but criticized the consideration of a 100-year payback scenario, arguing that  it underestimated land conversion effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP0506_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-WP0506-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHsummary_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-PHsummary-87">[87]</a></sup> American corn growers, biodiesel producers, ethanol producers and Brazilian sugarcane ethanol producers complained about EPA's methodology,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHsummary_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-PHsummary-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> while the oil industry requested an  implementation delay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHsummary_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-PHsummary-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 26, 2009, the House of Representatives approved the <a href="/wiki/American_Clean_Energy_and_Security_Act" title="American Clean Energy and Security Act">American Clean Energy and Security Act</a> 219 to 212, mandating EPA to exclude ILUC for a 5-year period, vis a vis RFS2. During this period, more research is to be conducted to develop more reliable models and methodologies for estimating ILUC, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">Congress</a> will review this issue before allowing EPA to rule on this matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The bill failed in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" title="U.S. Senate">U.S. Senate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 3, 2010, EPA issued its final RFS2 rule for 2010 and beyond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPARuling_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPARuling-39">[39]</a></sup> The rule incorporated direct and significant indirect emissions including ILUC. EPA incorporated comments and data from new studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA2010_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPA2010-40">[40]</a></sup> Using a 30-year time horizon and a 0% discount rate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAFinal2010_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAFinal2010-99">[99]</a></sup> EPA concluded that multiple biofuels would meet this standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>EPA's analysis accepted both <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_the_United_States" title="Ethanol fuel in the United States">ethanol produced from corn starch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Butanol_fuel" title="Butanol fuel">biobutanol</a> from corn starch as "renewable fuels". <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel_in_Brazil" title="Ethanol fuel in Brazil">Ethanol produced from sugarcane</a> became an "advanced fuel". Both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_diesel" title="Green diesel">diesel produced from algal oils</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> from soy oil and diesel from waste oils, fats, and greases fell in the "biomass-based diesel" category. <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">Cellulosic ethanol</a> and cellulosic diesel met the "cellulosic biofuel" standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA2010_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPA2010-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>The table summarizes the mean GHG emissions estimated by EPA modelling and the range of variations considering that the main source of uncertainty in the life cycle analysis is the GHG emissions related to international land use change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAFinal2010_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPAFinal2010-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>UNICA welcomed the ruling, in particular, for the more precise lifecycle emissions estimate and  hoped that classification the advanced biofuel designation would help eliminate the tariff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICA022010_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICA022010-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Fuels_Association" title="Renewable Fuels Association">Renewable Fuels Association</a> (RFA) also welcomed the ruling, as ethanol producers "require stable federal policy that provides them the market assurances they need to commercialize new technologies", restating their ILUC objection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA012010_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-RFA012010-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>RFA also complained that corn-based ethanol scored only a 21% reduction, noting that without ILUC, corn ethanol achieves a 52% GHG reduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA012010_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-RFA012010-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEPA010_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEPA010-104">[104]</a></sup> RFA also objected that Brazilian sugarcane ethanol "benefited disproportionally" because EPA's revisions lowered the initially equal ILUC estimates by half for corn and 93% for sugarcane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RFA022010_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-RFA022010-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern</a> lawmakers commented that they continued to oppose EPA's consideration of the "dicey science" of indirect land use that "punishes domestic fuels".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEPA010_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEPA010-104">[104]</a></sup> House Agriculture Chairman <a href="/wiki/Collin_Peterson" title="Collin Peterson">Collin Peterson</a> said, "... to think that we can credibly measure the impact of international indirect land use is completely unrealistic, and I will continue to push for legislation that prevents unreliable methods and unfair standards from burdening the biofuels industry."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEPA010_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEPA010-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>EPA Administrator <a href="/wiki/Lisa_P._Jackson" title="Lisa P. Jackson">Lisa P. Jackson</a> commented that the agency "did not back down from considering land use in its final rules, but the agency took new information into account that led to a more favorable calculation for ethanol".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEPA010_104-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEPA010-104">[104]</a></sup> She cited new science and better data on crop yield and productivity, more information on co-products that could be produced from advanced biofuels and expanded land-use data for 160 countries, instead of the 40 considered in the proposed rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEPA010_104-4"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEPA010-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010, European Union and United Kingdom regulators had recognized the need to take ILUC into account, but had not determined the most appropriate methodology.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_Renewable_Transport_Fuel_Obligation">UK Renewable Transport Fuel Obligation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: UK Renewable Transport Fuel Obligation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_transport_fuel_obligation" title="Renewable transport fuel obligation">Renewable transport fuel obligation</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">UK</a> <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Transport_Fuel_Obligation" title="Renewable Transport Fuel Obligation">Renewable Transport Fuel Obligation</a> (RTFO) program requires fuel suppliers to report direct impacts, and asked the <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Fuels_Agency" title="Renewable Fuels Agency">Renewable Fuels Agency</a> (RFA) to report potential indirect impacts, including ILUC and commodity price changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRTFO_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-UKRTFO-14">[14]</a></sup> The RFA's July 2008 "Gallager Review", mentioned several risks regarding biofuels and required feedstock production to avoid agricultural land that would otherwise be used for food production, despite concluding that "quantification of GHG emissions from indirect land-use change requires subjective assumptions and contains considerable uncertainty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher0708_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher0708-41">[41]</a></sup> Some environmental groups argued that emissions from ILUC were not being taken into account and could be creating more emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian0409_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian0409-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph0409_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph0409-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCNews0408_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNews0408-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Directive_on_the_Promotion_of_the_use_of_biofuels_and_other_renewable_fuels_for_transport" title="Directive on the Promotion of the use of biofuels and other renewable fuels for transport">Directive on the Promotion of the use of biofuels and other renewable fuels for transport</a></div>
<p>On December 17, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> approved the Renewable Energy Sources Directive (COM(2008)19) and amendments to the Fuel Quality Directive (Directive 2009/30),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> which included sustainability criteria for biofuels and mandated consideration of ILUC. The Directive established a 10% biofuel target. A separate Fuel Quality Directive set the <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_fuel_standard#EU_low-carbon_fuel_standard" title="Low-carbon fuel standard">EU's Low Carbon Fuel Standard</a>, requiring a 6% reduction in GHG intensity of EU transport fuels by 2020. The legislation ordered the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> to develop a methodology to factor in GHG emissions from ILUC by December 31, 2010, based on the best available scientific evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU08_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-EU08-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARBproposal_54-4"><a href="#cite_note-ARBproposal-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ILUC_EU_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-ILUC_EU-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the meantime, the European Parliament defined lands that were ineligible for producing biofuel feedstocks for the purpose of the Directives. This category included <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> and continuously <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forested</a> areas with <a href="/wiki/Canopy_(biology)" title="Canopy (biology)">canopy</a> cover of more than 30 percent or cover between 10 and 30 percent given evidence that its existing carbon stock was low enough to justify conversion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU08_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-EU08-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Commission subsequently published terms of reference for three ILUC modeling exercises: one using a General Equilibrium model;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> one using a Partial Equilibrium model<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> and one comparing other global modeling exercises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> It also consulted on a limited range of high-level options for addressing ILUC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> to which 17 countries<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and 59 organizations responded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur" title="United Nations Special Rapporteur">United Nations Special Rapporteur</a> on the Right to Food and several environmental organizations complained that the 2008 safeguards were inadequate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> UNICA called for regulators to establish an empirical and  "globally accepted methodology" to consider ILUC, with the participation of researchers and scientists from biofuel crop-producing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010 some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">NGOs</a> accused the European Commission of lacking transparency given its reluctance to release documents relating to the ILUC work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In March 2010 the Partial and General Equilibrium Modelling results were made available, with the disclaimer that the EC had not adopted the views contained in the materials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> These indicate that a 1.25% increase in EU biofuel consumption would require around 5,000,000 hectares (12,000,000 acres) of land globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUiluc_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUiluc-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>The scenarios for varied from 5.6-8.6% of road transport fuels. The study found that ILUC effects offset part of the emission benefits, and that above the 5.6% threshold, ILUC emissions increase rapidly increase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUilucPDF_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUilucPDF-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCCEU_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCCEU-126">[126]</a></sup> For the expected scenario of 5.6% by 2020, the study estimated that biodiesel production increases would be mostly domestic, while bioethanol production would take place mainly in Brazil, regardless of EU duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUilucPDF_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUilucPDF-125">[125]</a></sup> The analysis concluded that eliminating trade barriers would further reduce emissions, because the EU would import more from Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUiluc_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUiluc-124">[124]</a></sup> Under this scenario, "<i>direct emission savings from biofuels are estimated at 18 Mt <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>, additional emissions from ILUC at 5.3 Mt <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (mostly in Brazil), resulting in a global net balance of nearly 13 Mt <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> savings in a 20 years horizon.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUilucPDF_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-EUilucPDF-125">[125]</a></sup> The study also found that ILUC emissions were much greater for biodiesel from <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_oil" title="Vegetable oil">vegetable oil</a> and estimated that in 2020 even at the 5.6% level were over half the greenhouse gas emissions from diesel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUilucPDF_125-3"><a href="#cite_note-EUilucPDF-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCCEU_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-GCCEU-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of the announcement, the Commission stated that it would publish a report on ILUC by the end of 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC0610_2_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC0610_2-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Certification_system">Certification system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Certification system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>On June 10, 2010, the EC announced its decision to set up certification schemes for biofuels, including imports as part of the Renewable Energy Directive. The Commission encouraged E.U. nations, industry and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">NGOs</a> to set up voluntary certification schemes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC0610_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC0610-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0610_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCC0610-129">[129]</a></sup> EC figures for 2007 showed that 26% of <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> and 31% of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">bioethanol</a> used in the E.U. was imported, mainly from <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC0610_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC0610-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_2">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>UNICA welcomed the EU efforts to "engage independent experts in its assessments" but requested  that improvements because "... the report currently contains a certain number of inaccuracies, so once these are corrected, we anticipate even higher benefits resulting from the use of Brazilian sugarcane ethanol."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICAEU10_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICAEU10-131">[131]</a></sup> UNICA highlighted the fact that the report assumed land expansion that "does not take into consideration the agro-ecological zoning for sugarcane in Brazil, which prevents cane from expanding into any type of native vegetation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICAEU10_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNICAEU10-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Critics said the 10% figure was reduced to 5.6% of transport fuels partly by exaggerating the contribution of <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> (EV) in 2020, as the study assumed EVs would represent 20% of new car sales, two and six times the car industry's own estimate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReutersEU10_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersEU10-132">[132]</a></sup> They also claimed the study "exaggerates to around 45 percent the contribution of bioethanol—the greenest of all biofuels—and consequently downplays the worst impacts of biodiesel."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReutersEU10_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersEU10-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>Environmental groups found that the measures "are too weak to halt a dramatic increase in deforestation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC0610_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC0610-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenpeace0610_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace0610-133">[133]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>, "indirect land-use change impacts of biofuel production still are not properly addressed", which for them was the most dangerous problem of biofuels<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenpeace0610_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greenpeace0610-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>Industry representatives welcomed the certification system and some dismissed concerns regarding the lack of land use criteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC0610_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-BBC0610-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0610_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0610-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unica0610_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Unica0610-135">[135]</a></sup> UNICA and other industry groups wanted the gaps in the rules filled to provide a clear operating framework.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT0610_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0610-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Unica0610_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Unica0610-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p><p>The negotiations between the European Parliament and the Council of European Ministers continue. A deal is not foreseen before 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Indirect_land_use_change_impacts_of_biofuels&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-Sawyer08-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Sawyer08_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Donald Sawyer (2008-05-27). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2373893" rel="nofollow">"Climate change, biofuels and eco-social impacts in the Brazilian Amazon and Cerrado"</a>.
